Q: Which Gilbert and Sullivan opera has the alternate title 'The Peer and the Peri'? A: Iolanthe
Q: In the Asterix books, what is the name of Asterix's closest friend? A: Obelix
Q: Which girl group took 'Manic Monday' to Number two in the UK charts in 1986? A: The Bangles
Q: The site of Pompeii is dose to which city, the capital of Italy's Campania region? A: Naples
Q: What is the name of the 1971 Spielberg film which pits Dennis Weaver against an unseen truck driver? A: Duel
Q: In Greek mythology, who killed Medusa while looking at her in a mirror-like shield? A: Perseus
Q: According to the New Testament, on which Mediterranean island did St John write the Book of Revelation? A: Patmos
Q: In heraldry what is a martlet? A: Bird
Q: Which singer/actress founded Maverick Records in 1992? A: Madonna
Q: In the TV series 'Rising Damp' what was the name of Rigsby's cat? A: Vienna
Q: What is the NATO phonetic alphabet call sign for the letter M? A: Mike
Q: What was the codename for the British/American landings in French North Africa, begun in November 1942? A: Operation Torch
Q: Which musical instrument did Tommy Dorsey play? A: Trombone
Q: What is the name of the Adobe software that is used to create PDF (portable document format) files? A: Acrobat
Q: In which Bond film does Claudine Auger play Domino? A: Thunderball
Q: What is the title of the signature tune, composed by Arthur Wood, of Radio 4's programme 'The Archers'? A: Barwick Green
Q: Originally manufactured by Peek Freans, these biscuits were named after which patriot and soldier, following his visit to the UK in 1854? A: Garibaldi
Q: In The Pickwick Papers, what is the name of Pickwick's landlady who sues him for breach of promise? A: Mrs Bardell
Q: Which Shipping Forecast area lies south of Sole? A: Fitzroy
Q: In the Asterix books, what is the name of the 93-year-old, oldest inhabitant of the village? A: Geriatrix
Q: Which girl group took 'Robert de Niro's Waiting' to Number 3 in the UK pop charts of 1984? A: Bananarama
Q: How many symphonies did Johannes Brahms write? A: Four
Q: Which artist created 'The Lobster Telephone' in 1936 and 'Mae West Lip Sofa' in 1937? A: Salvador Dali
Q: For which film did Steven Spielberg win his first Oscar for Best Director? A: Schindler's List
Q: According to Greek mythology who killed Achilles by shooting him in the heel with a poisoned arrow? A: Paris
Q: According to Acts in the New Testament, on which Mediterranean island was St Paul shipwrecked? A: Malta
Q: In heraldry what is a mullet? A: (Five pointed) Star
Q: Of what is pogonology the study? A: Beards
Q: Who invented the 'cat's eye' road safety device in 1934? A: Percy Shaw
Q: What was the real name of 'Phiz', the illustrator of some of Charles Dickens' works? A: (Hablot Knight) Browne
Q: Who wrote the novel Villette' in 1853? A: Charlotte Bronte
Q: In the TV series 'Rising Damp', which actress played Miss Jones? A: Frances de la Tour
Q: "The line ""That's not the Northern Lights, that's Manderley"" is said towards the end of which 1940 film?" A: Rebecca
Q: What is the NATO phonetic alphabet call for Q? A: Quebec
Q: What type of exhibits can be seen in the museum at Crich in Derbyshire? A: Trams
Q: What was the codename for the German invasion of the Soviet Union in June 1941? A: Operation Barbarossa
Q: Which musical instrument did Bix Beiderbecke play? A: Cornet
Q: By what name is Allen Stewart Konigsberg better known? A: Woody Allen
Q: Who wrote the 1845 poem 'Home Thoughts from Abroad'? A: Robert Browning
Q: Which Daphne du Maurier novel is centred around a coaching house on Bodmin Moor? A: Jamaica Inn
